<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

The Segmented-Line Non-uniformly Distributed-Turns Coil (SL-NDTC) uses non-uniformly distributed turns radii that have been optimized for reactive and radiative read performance. This leads to a dual purpose near- and far-field antenna in a single unit. Simulations show a more focused magnetic-field (H-field) distribution in the near field of the SL-NDTC compared to more conventional coils. Single and dual turn designs are compared to the SL-NDTC antenna to evidence enhanced near- and far-field performance in the latter.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID) has attracted considerable attention recently. This technology contactlessly shares information between an Interrogator (Reader) and a Transponder (Tag) when tuned to a common frequency of operation. Near-field RFID employs inductive coupling between the Tag and the Reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, and operates in the Low Frequency (LF) and High Frequency (HF) bands. Solid-line unsegmented coils are conventionally used for low-cost interrogator and tag designs <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. UHF 840-960 MHz RFID is typically used in the far-field for read distances of several meters, but for item-level identification in healthcare (e.g. bio-sensing), medical instrumentation, and real-time logistics (e.g. track-and-trace) of mobile consumables (e.g. medicines) and patients, near-field is used <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. Therefore, both the reactive near-field or radiated electromagnetic (EM) far-field may be utilized at UHF depending on the application and dual purpose near- and far-field UHF-RFID antennas are sought. For such an antenna to work at UHF, the challenge is to reuse conventional inductive coupling LF/HF designs, since they possess relatively large electrical dimensions at 900 MHz. Yet, a uniform current distribution along the length of the antenna must also be maintained for near-field operations where a strong magnetic (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) field is required in the inductive zone. Therefore, the coil, which can be electrically large at UHF, must be modified to remove current phasing effects. LF- and HF-RFID inductive coupling solid-line coil antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> can be adapted for this dual read range performance at UHF. The coils reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> are quite small at LH/HF, having loop lengths in the order of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="width: 2.345em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.04em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\lambda /10</script></tex-math></inline-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-11" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the operating wavelength. They can support in-phase current flow around the coil with consistent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-14" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the near-field <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. However, such a coil used at UHF would require phase compensation to establish an appropriate current distribution since the loop length becomes comparable to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-17" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-18"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (i.e. it is electrically large) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. Therefore, the modal pattern on the loop caused by phase progression in the current flow needs to be removed since the solid-line UHF coil would suffer from a non-uniform <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-20" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-21"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the NF interrogation zone and lead to poor coupling.</p><p>Reinforcement of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-23" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by segmenting the conducting line of a coil antenna with lumped capacitors was reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> where broken-loop antennas formed of multiple line segments using capacitive couplers were described. In essence, these couplers offer appropriate phase shifts to cause the individual <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-26" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula> contributions of each segment to sum constructively <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>. For realization, various segmented-line configurations exist, e.g., dashed-line <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, embedded phase shifters <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, and distributed capacitors <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> where regardless of the coils being electrically large, a co-phased current flow is maintained. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a>, segmented-line coils using distributed fork-shaped capacitors were preferred owing to their relatively straightforward implementation, and in this letter, the authors describe the Segmented-Line Single-Turn Coil (SL-STC) from <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a> for comparison with a conventional Single Turn Coil STC; the antennas however do not use conventional reflectors. Multi-turn coils are also of interest since they can substantially enhance the inductive coupling between a Reader and Tag antenna. In this paper, a dual purpose near- and far-field UHF-RFID antenna coil consisting of segmented-lines in a multi-turn fashion is presented for the first time. This segmented-line coil antenna with non-uniformly distributed turns and fork-shaped capacitors is evolved from an earlier reported solid-line Non-uniformly Distributed-Turns Coil (NDTC) antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a> and the segmented version of this design will be shown to exhibit an enhanced near-field <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-29" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula> while also performing acceptably in the far-field.</p><p>The paper is organized as follows. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> describes the SL-STC coil from <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a> and a conventional STC antenna is also given for comparison purposes. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2a" class="fulltext-link">Section II-A</a> presents the proposed SL-NDTC antenna design with optimized turn radii. Simulated results are given to validate the design in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> and the paper is concluded in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Segmented-Line Coil Design</h2></div><p>A conventional STC antenna is presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>, and the SL-STC with distributed fork capacitors <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a> is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>. The coils are etched on an FR4 substrate of thickness, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-32" role="math" style="width: 5.769em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.168em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.17em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-33"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-34" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.8</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-37" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-38"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-40" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">h = 0.8~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, relative dielectric constant <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-41" role="math" style="width: 3.847em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.426em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.43em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-44"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.36em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-46" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϵ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-47" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-48" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-49" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">4.4</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">{\epsilon _r} = 4.4</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and loss tangent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-50" role="math" style="width: 5.829em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.228em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.17em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-51"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-52" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">tan</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-53"></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-54" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.183em;">δ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-55" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.02</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">\tan \delta = 0.02</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The coil lies in the x-y plane with its center at the coordinate origin and consists of copper tracks of width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-57" role="math" style="width: 4.808em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.327em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.33em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-58"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-59" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-60" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-61" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-62" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-63"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-64"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-65" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">d = 1~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and radius <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-66" role="math" style="width: 6.129em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.529em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1005.53em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-67"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-68"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-69"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-70"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-71" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-72" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-73" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-74" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">75</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-75" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-76"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-77"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-78" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">{R_1} = 75~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as with the design in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a>. The STC [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>] and the SL-STC [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>] both have an electrically large perimeter of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-79" role="math" style="width: 2.646em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.345em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.35em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-80"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-81" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">1.44</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-82" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">1.44\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the resonant frequency of 915 MHz, and a segmented line is introduced to allow unidirectional current flow in the latter. In order to cause the current in each short segment to be co-phased at the resonant frequency, the length of each segment including the capacitor is 39.27 mm; that led to a total amount of 11 capacitors [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>]. Each segment, includes a known fork-shaped capacitor from <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a>, was found iteratively by adjusting the phase shifts with segment length. The total number of capacitors is therefore given by dividing the coil's total track length by one segment length. Finally the coil is matched to 50<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-83" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-84"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-85" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> using a stub matching circuit which lies on the front and back of the substrate. To demonstrate enhancement of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-86" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-87"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-88" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the near-field, 2 and 4 turn non-uniformly distributed coils were designed subsequently.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>(a) stc and (b) SL-stc antennas.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7046270/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Proposed SL-NDTC Antenna Design</h3><p>The SL-NDTC antenna, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>, is segmented by a number of equally distributed fork-shaped capacitors over <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-89" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> turns with respective radii <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-92" role="math" style="width: 6.069em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.468em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.35em 2.646em -999.997em); As for the SL-STC, the SL-NDTC has 39.27 mm long segments and this length is maintained across the connections between turns to facilitate a co-phased current flow in the coil; that led to a total amount of 34 capacitors. <p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Results</h2></div><p>The coil antennas described in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> were evaluated for 1 W input power using Zeland IE3D, based on the Method of Moments (MoM).</p><p>The S11 responses of the coils are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-269" role="math" style="width: 3.667em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.25em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-270"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-271" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-272" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-273" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-274"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-275"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-276" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">-10~\hbox{dB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> Bandwidths (BW) are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> for the operating frequency of 915 MHz. The coils considered are the STC, the SL-STC, the SL-NDTC and a Segmented Line-Dual Turn Coil (SL-DTC) with the geometry shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> which was created to provide an intermediate result between the SL-STC and the SL-NDTC.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>S11 of the UHF-rfid coil antennas.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7046270/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>SL-dtc antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7046270/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Simulated bandwidths of the considered designs<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> indicates that wide fractional bandwidths between 18% and 25% can be obtained for the multi-turn segmented designs which are 5–7 times greater than for the single turn, non-segmented coil. The achieved bandwidths are influenced by the double stub matching networks (inset <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 2</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">4</a>) meaning that the quoted values may not be the maximum obtainable in each case. However, as the proposed SL-NDTC fully covers the 865-868 MHz (Europe) and 902-928 MHz (North America) UHF industrial, scientific and medical ISM radio bands, further improvement was not deemed necessary.</p><p>The SL-DTC of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> was obtained by an iterative procedure to establish appropriate separation between turns. Starting with a fixed <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-277" role="math" style="width: 6.129em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.529em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1005.53em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-278"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-279"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-280"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-281"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-282" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-283" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-284" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-285" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">75</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-286" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-287"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-288"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-289" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">{R_1} = 75~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> similar to the STC antenna, the radius of the second turn was found by optimization from the iterative radii shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. By observation, the response for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-290" role="math" style="width: 4.027em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.607em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.61em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-291"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-292"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-293"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-294"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-295" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-296" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-297" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-298" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">57</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">{R_2} = 57</script></tex-math></inline-formula> achieved the highest <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-299" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-301"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-302"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-303"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-304" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-305" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">{H_z}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The required stub matching circuit (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> inset) for the SL-DTC design was also found by iteration to have values <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-306" role="math" style="width: 6.429em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.769em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.77em 2.526em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.303em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-312" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-313" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-314" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">4.48</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-315" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-316"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-317"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-318" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{l_1} = 4.48~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-319" role="math" style="width: 6.429em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.769em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.77em 2.526em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.303em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-325" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-326" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-327" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.303em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-338" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-339" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-340" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-341" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-342"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-343"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-344" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; Further turns of the SL coil were added and assessed similarly leading to the final SL-NDTC design.

<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7046270/7046270-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Simulated currents (a) and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-345" role="math" style="width: 1.128em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.863em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.86em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-346"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-347" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution (b) of the coils using 1 w input power.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7046270/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The simulated current flow and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-348" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-349"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-350"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-351"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-352"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-353" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-354" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">{H_z}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution of the coils at 915 MHz are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6(a) and (b)</a> respectively. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-355" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-356"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-357"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-358"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-359"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-360" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-361" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">{H_z}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distributions are displayed in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-362" role="math" style="width: 5.288em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.748em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1004.75em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-363"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-364"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-365"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-366" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-367" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-368" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">50</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-369" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-370"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-371"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-372" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">{\rm z}=50~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> plane. Due to the electrically large loop length in the STC antenna, oppositely directed current flow is observed which led to current phase cancellations for reverse currents. For the SL-STC design, the currents contributed constructively in the x-y plane and resulted in a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-373" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-374"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-375"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-376"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-377"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-378" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-379" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">{H_z}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> field peak of magnitude 0.37 A/m in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-380" role="math" style="width: 5.288em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.748em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1004.75em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-381"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-382"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-383"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-384" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-385" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-386" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">50</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-387" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-388"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-389"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-390" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">{\rm z}=50~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> plane which is twice that of the STC. For the intermediate 2 turn SL-DTC design, the current flow in the inner turn has the same direction as for the outer turn, contributing constructively so that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-391" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-392"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-393"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-394"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-395"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-396" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-397" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">{H_z}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> becomes 0.45 A/m which is 1.2 times greater than the SL-STC. Finally, the constructive contribution of currents flowing in the SL-NDTC produces <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-398" role="math" style="width: 3.066em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.71em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-399"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-400"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-401"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-402"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-403" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-404" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-405" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-406" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">1.3</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">{H_z}\ 1.3</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 1.57 and 3.3 times higher than the SL-DTC, SL-STC and the STC respectively. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> shows the simulated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-407" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-469" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.586em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.53em 2.405em -999.997em); Far-Field Results</h3><p>To assess the SL-NDTC for far-field UHF RFID application, the antenna was measured in an anechoic chamber in far-field. The measured radiation patterns are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> while the simulated efficiency and gain are plotted with frequency in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>. The far-field results show the proposed SL-NDTC antenna has a gain of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-474" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-475"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-476" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">∼</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-477" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.4</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-478" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-479"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-480"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-481" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dBi</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\sim 1.4~\hbox{dBi}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and an efficiency of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-482" role="math" style="width: 3.246em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.886em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.83em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-483"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-484" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">∼</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-485" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">80</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-486" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">%</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">\sim 80\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. There is a reasonably flat gain response across 840-960 MHz with a slight variation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-487" role="math" style="width: 6.79em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.129em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.13em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-488"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-489" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-490"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-491"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-492" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-493" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-494" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">0.05</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-495" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-496"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-497"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-498" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dBi</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">+/- 0.05~\hbox{dBi}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The radiation patterns are similar in co-pol and x-pol of the Elevation and Azimuth planes, and have a relatively wide E-total coverage. This indicates a potential for interrogation of tags in any orientation.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this letter, an original dual purpose near- and far-field UHF-RFID coil antenna with non-uniformly distributed-turns and segmented-lines has been presented. The proposed antenna performs well in the reactive and radiated read zones and is implemented as a 2 layer pcb requiring just 2 vias. Co-phasing of incremental current segments in non-uniformly distributed turns was shown to lead to an enhanced magnetic near-field. The proposed antenna had a simulated efficiency of 80% in the far-field with a directivity that remained stable across the UHF-RFID band. Wide radiation patterns were obtained in the Azimuth plane and the co-pol and x-pol components were similar. The antenna therefore is a good UHF-RFID interrogator candidate for near and far field applications with potential to read tags in any orientation. Although this does not guarantee that all the tags are read in the far-field, the wide E-total radiation pattern can in theory allow reception, depending on the receiver sensitivity, from any orientation.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
